      <a href="/wiki/Happy_Xmas_(War_Is_Over)" title="Happy Xmas (War Is Over)">
       Happy Xmas (War Is Over)
      </a>
      ", released on 8 December that year.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Listen50_10-11">
       <a href="#cite_note-Listen50-10">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        10
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Cover_versions_and_cultural_references">
       Cover versions and cultural references
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Instant_Karma!&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Cover versions and cultural references">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Artists who have covered "Instant Karma!" include
      <a href="/wiki/Toad_the_Wet_Sprocket" title="Toad the Wet Sprocket">
       Toad the Wet Sprocket
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123">
       <a href="#cite_note-123">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        114
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Paul_Weller" title="Paul Weller">
       Paul Weller
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124">
       <a href="#cite_note-124">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        115
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Duran_Duran" title="Duran Duran">
       Duran Duran
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">
       <a href="#cite_note-125">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        116
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tater_Totz" title="Tater Totz">
       Tater Totz
      </a>
      with
      <a href="/wiki/Cherie_Currie" title="Cherie Currie">
       Cherie Currie
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126">
       <a href="#cite_note-126">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        117
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Tokio_Hotel" title="Tokio Hotel">
       Tokio Hotel
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127">
       <a href="#cite_note-127">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        118
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2007, the song provided the title for
      <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">
       Amnesty International
      </a>
      's multi-artist compilation of Lennon compositions,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Instant_Karma:_The_Amnesty_International_Campaign_to_Save_Darfur" title="Instant Karma: The Amnesty International Campaign to Save Darfur">
        Instant Karma: The Amnesty International Campaign to Save Darfur
       </a>
      </i>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128">
       <a href="#cite_note-128">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        119
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      for which
      <a href="/wiki/U2" title="U2">
       U2
      </a>
      recorded a cover version.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129">
       <a href="#cite_note-129">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        120
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The title of
      <a href="/wiki/Stephen_King" title="Stephen King">
       Stephen King
      </a>
      's horror novel
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Shining_(novel)" title="The Shining (novel)">
        The Shining
       </a>
      </i>
      (1977) came from Lennon's line "
      <i>
       We all shine on
      </i>
      " King has said that he was going to call the book
      <i>
       The Shine
      </i>
      , before realising that "shine" had been used as a derogatory term for black people.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130">
       <a href="#cite_note-130">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        121
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1988,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131">
       <a href="#cite_note-131">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        122
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Ono allowed the footwear and apparel company
      <a href="/wiki/Nike,_Inc." title="Nike, Inc.">
       Nike
      </a>
      to feature "Instant Karma!" in an advertising campaign, after a public outcry the previous year had forced her to withdraw permission for the use of Lennon's Beatles composition "
      <a href="/wiki/Revolution_(Beatles_song)" title="Revolution (Beatles song)">
       Revolution
      </a>
      ".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132">
       <a href="#cite_note-132">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        123
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Instant_Karma_(record_label)" title="Instant Karma (record label)">
       Instant Karma Records
      </a>
      was named after the song,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133">
       <a href="#cite_note-133">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        124
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/The_Flaming_Lips" title="The Flaming Lips">
       the Flaming Lips
      </a>
      recorded their track "I Don't Understand Karma" in 2009 as a reply to "Instant Karma!"
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134">
       <a href="#cite_note-134">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        125
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Personnel">
       Personnel
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">

       </span>

       </a>

        ]
       </span>

     <p>
      The following musicians contributed to the recording of "Instant Karma!":
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-C.26P_p_171_46-3">

      <li>

       </a>
       
       <a href="/wiki/Lead_vocalist" title="Lead vocalist">

       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Acoustic_guitar" title="Acoustic guitar">

       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Piano" title="Piano">
        piano
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Williams_p_143_38-3">

         </span>

         <span>
          ]

        </a>
       </sup>

       </a>

       </a>
       
       <a href="/wiki/Electric_guitar" title="Electric guitar">

       </a>
       , piano, backing vocal
      </li>

       </a>
       
       <a href="/wiki/Bass_guitar" title="Bass guitar">
        bass guitar
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Electric_piano" title="Electric piano">
        electric piano
       </a>
       , backing vocal
      </li>
      <li>

       , piano, backing vocal

       </a>
       , backing vocal

       </a>

       </a>

       </a>
       and several dozen revellers from London's Hatchett Club  backing vocals

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">
       Notes
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Instant_Karma!&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Notes">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="reflist columns references-column-count references-column-count-2" style="-moz-column-count: 2; -webkit-column-count: 2; column-count: 2; list-style-type: decimal;">
      <ol class="references">
       <li id="cite_note-20">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-20">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         In an interview with New York radio station
         <a href="/wiki/WPLJ" title="WPLJ">
          WPLJ
         </a>
         , Lennon said that he had "stole[n] the introduction" from "Some Other Guy".
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
          <a href="#cite_note-19">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           19
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-47">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-47">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Although authors such as
         <a href="/wiki/Richard_Williams_(journalist)" title="Richard Williams (journalist)">
          Richard Williams
         </a>
         ,
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Williams_p_143_38-2">
          <a href="#cite_note-Williams_p_143-38">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           37
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
         <a href="/wiki/Mick_Brown_(journalist)" title="Mick Brown (journalist)">
          Mick Brown
         </a>
         ,
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brown_p_242_44-1">
          <a href="#cite_note-Brown_p_242-44">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           43
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
         <a href="/wiki/Mark_Lewisohn" title="Mark Lewisohn">
          Mark Lewisohn
         </a>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Madinger_.26_Easter_p_33_2-4">
          <a href="#cite_note-Madinger_.26_Easter_p_33-2">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           2
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
         and Ribowsky
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ribowsky_p_252_45-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-Ribowsky_p_252-45">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           44
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
         state that Lennon played piano, some sources give electric piano as his keyboard instrument on the song.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Spizer_p_28_32-3">
          <a href="#cite_note-Spizer_p_28-32">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           31
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-C.26P_p_171_46-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-C.26P_p_171-46">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           45
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-56">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-56">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Lennon and Harrison had long been admirers of Spector's work in the 1960s,
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Woffinden_p_31_28-1">
          <a href="#cite_note-Woffinden_p_31-28">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           27
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
         with
         <a href="/wiki/The_Ronettes" title="The Ronettes">
          the Ronettes
         </a>
         and other vocal groups.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
          <a href="#cite_note-54">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           52
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
         Lennon later explained that the Beatles had discussed using Spector before 1970 as an alternative to their usual producer,
         <a href="/wiki/George_Martin" title="George Martin">
          George Martin
         </a>
         .
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
          <a href="#cite_note-55">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           53
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-65">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-65">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         The single's catalog number was Apple 1003 in the UK and Apple 1818 in America.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
          <a href="#cite_note-64">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           61
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-73">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-73">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Author
         <a href="/wiki/Jon_Wiener" title="Jon Wiener">
          Jon Wiener
         </a>
         also writes of the media's disinterest in the couple by the end of 1969, and quotes Apple executive
         <a href="/wiki/Peter_Brown_(music_industry)" title="Peter Brown (music industry)">
          Peter Brown
         </a>
         's assertion that Lennon's new adopted cause "destroyed his last shred of credibility with the press".
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
          <a href="#cite_note-72">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           68
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-75">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-75">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         As with the press conference with Michael X, the Lennons' rehearsals and performances for
         <i>
          Tops of the Pops
         </i>
         were simultaneously filmed by Tony Cox for a possible
         <a href="/wiki/Documentary_film" title="Documentary film">
          documentary film
         </a>
         on the couple.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Madinger_.26_Easter_p_34_74-2">
          <a href="#cite_note-Madinger_.26_Easter_p_34-74">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           69
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-83">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-83">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         On the US listings compiled by
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Cashbox_(magazine)" title="Cashbox (magazine)">
           Cash Box
          </a>
         </i>
         and
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Record_World" title="Record World">
           Record World
          </a>
         </i>
         magazines, it also peaked at number 3,
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Spizer_p_27_81-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-Spizer_p_27-81">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           75
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
         while Britain's
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Melody_Maker" title="Melody Maker">
           Melody Maker
          </a>
         </i>
         chart recorded the song at number 4.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
          <a href="#cite_note-82">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           76
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-89">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-89">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         The award came on the same day that Harrison's debut single, "
         <a href="/wiki/My_Sweet_Lord" title="My Sweet Lord">
          My Sweet Lord
         </a>
         ", was certified gold by the RIAA,
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-C.26P_p_332_87-1">
          <a href="#cite_note-C.26P_p_332-87">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           80
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
         yet that song's US release took place nine months after "Instant Karma!"
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
          <a href="#cite_note-88">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           81
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-113">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-113">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Apple's artwork for
         <i>
          Shaved Fish
         </i>
         featured an illustration by Michael Bryan for each of the compilation's tracks. "Instant Karma!" is depicted as a jar of instant coffee, with the top removed and a spoon beside the jar.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">
          <a href="#cite_note-112">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           104
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
        </span>
       </li>
      </ol>
     </div>
